## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling (materials science)
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship of a material, a core problem in solid mechanics and materials science. Temperature typically modifies the elastic modulus and flow stress, while strain determines the deformation response through linear or nonlinear constitutive laws.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law (temperature-independent): sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elastic, constant temperature)
- Temperature-dependent linear elasticity: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 - T) (elastic modulus decreasing linearly with temperature)
- Temperature-dependent elasticity (normalized): sigma = c0 * epsilon * (1 - c1 * T) (linear thermal softening of modulus)
- Polynomial thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (1 - c1 * T + c2 * T**2) (quadratic temperature dependence of modulus)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (nonlinear stress-strain without temperature effect)
- Power-law hardening with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (1 - c2 * T) (combined nonlinear strain and linear thermal softening)
- Johnson-Cook type (no strain rate): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 - c3 * T**c4) (hardening with thermal softening)
- Arrhenius thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon * exp(c1 * T) (exponential temperature dependence of modulus)
- Arrhenius-type with power-law strain: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (thermally activated deformation with hardening)
- Voce hardening with temperature: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) * (1 - c2 * T) (saturating hardening with thermal softening)
- Ramberg-Osgood inverse form: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2 (linear + power-law nonlinear terms)
- Hyperbolic sine flow stress: sigma = c0 * T * asinh(c1 * epsilon) (sinh-law constitutive model)
- Combined linear and thermal: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon * T (strain-temperature coupling)
- Rational temperature dependence: sigma = c0 * epsilon * c1 / (T + c2) (modulus with rational T dependence)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear thermal softening of elastic modulus → multiplicative factor (1 - c*T) or (c0 - c1*T) multiplying strain terms
- Homologous temperature scaling → temperature appears as ratio T/c (normalized by melting temperature), equivalent to c*T
- Strain hardening saturation → exponential approach to limit: c0*(1 - exp(-c1*epsilon)), indicating dislocation density saturation
- Thermally activated processes → Arrhenius-type exp(c/T) or exp(-c*T) terms reflecting activation energy barriers
- Separable strain-temperature structure → sigma = f(epsilon) * g(T), where strain and temperature effects are multiplicatively separable
- Elastic-plastic transition → sum of linear and power-law terms: c0*epsilon + c1*epsilon**c2, capturing yield and hardening
- High-temperature creep regime → inverse or negative power of T multiplying strain terms, reflecting diffusion-controlled deformation
- Polynomial modulus correction → E(T) expressed as polynomial in T (quadratic or cubic) multiplied by strain
